## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of population change (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size. This is a fundamental problem in population ecology where various growth models (exponential, logistic, Allee effect, etc.) describe how populations grow, saturate, or decline based on density-dependent and time-dependent factors.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreases logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density but no critical threshold)
- Linear density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (quadratic population model)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible sigmoidal growth)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth rate)
- Exponential with time-varying rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (time-dependent intrinsic growth rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (hyperbolic density dependence)
- Cubic population model: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP/dt is proportional to P at low densities but curves downward at high P → logistic or rational density dependence (c0*P*(1-c1*P) or c0*P/(1+c1*P))
- If dP/dt is negative for both very small and very large P → Allee effect with cubic structure P*(P-a)*(K-P)
- If dP/dt shows asymmetric sigmoidal behavior relative to P → Gompertz or theta-logistic with non-unity exponent
- If dP/dt depends explicitly on time t → environmental forcing, seasonal modulation, or non-autonomous dynamics (often sinusoidal or exponential in t)
- If dP/dt = 0 at exactly one nonzero P value → single stable equilibrium (logistic-type); if at two nonzero values → bistability (Allee-type)
- If the relationship between dP/dt/P and P is linear → classic logistic model; if curved → generalized models needed
- If dP/dt scales as a power law of P (not linear) → Von Bertalanffy or allometric growth models with P**c exponents
- If dP/dt has periodic fluctuations with t while maintaining P-dependence → multiplicative separation of variables f(P)*g(t)
